[ب] والثاني أن القسمة يدل على تقرير كل فصل مع جنس فوقه جنسا لما تحته فجرى ترتيب الفصول على التوالي حتى يكون ما يجتمع من الفصول إنما يجتمع على تواليها؛ فلا يذهب منها شيء في الوسط. فإذا أريد أن يركب الحد من الأنواع إلى الأجناس لم يظفر من نوع إلى جنس أبعد بل الجنس الذي يليه . [ت] والثالث أنها إذا وفيت على الواجب كانت تشتمل على الفصول الذاتية كلها فلا يبقى شيء منها فيكون قد أعطيت الفصول على تواليها طولا؛ ولو عرضًا فإنه يمكن أن يقسم الجنس بقسمين ليس أحدهما تحت الآخر مثل الجسم ذي النفس إلى المتحرك بالإرادة وغير المتحرك بالإرادة، وإلى الحسّاس وغير الحسّاس مرة؛ فيجب أن يكون مراعيًا لهذا في القسمة عرضًا كما يجب طولا كيلا يفوت فصل من فصول يقسم إلى فصول ذاتية متداخلة أو متوافقة. والمتداخلة مثل المائت وغير المائت، والناطق وغير الناطق المتوافقة مثل الحسّاس وغير الحسّاس، والمتحرك بالإرادة وغير المتحرك بالإرادة.
والقانون في مراعاة الوجه الثاني والثالث هو أن تكون القسمة بالذاتيات المقومات للأنواع، وأن تكون القسمة قسمة أولية للجنس وهي القسمة التي يكون للجنس في القسمة التي للجنس من طريق ما هو جنس مثلا يجب أن يقسم الحيوان أولا إلى الطائر والسابح والزاحف والماشي: ثم يقسم الماشي إلى ذي رجلين وذي الأرجل، والطائر إلى متصل الجناح ومنفصل الجناح. فإن أحل بهذا وقسم الحيوان أولا إلى متصل الجناح ومنفصل الجناح فما قسم الحيوان من جهة ما هو حيوان بل من جهة ما هو طائر. وكذلك إذا قسم الحيوان إلى ذي الأرجل وذي رجلين فإنه ما قسّم من جهة ما هو حيوان بل من جهة ما هو ماشي فيجب أن ينظر هل يحتاج الجنس / إلى أن تصير له [٣١٦] طبيعة زائدة على طبيعة الجنسية حتى تقبل هذه القسمة، أو لا يحتاج بل وهذه القسمة له أولا؛ فتقدم القسمة التي تكون أولا، وتؤخّر القسمة التي لا تكون أولا . فإذا قسم قسمة أولية جميع المقسوم والفصل؛ ثم قسم قسمة أولية أخرى. وكذلك إلى أن ينتهي إلى ما لا ينقسم إلا بالعدد. وبالجملة يجب أن تكون الفصول ذاتية في القسمة؛ وبيان كيفية تلك القسمة قد مرَّ، ولا يلزم أن يكون واحد منها معلومًا.
وقد قيل في التعليم الأول لا كل المنقسم يضطر في تقسيمه، ولا المحدد في تحديده إلى أن يعلم كل شيء على ما ظن بعضهم بل يلزم أن يراعي في القسمة النافعة في التحديد أعراضًا ثلاثة [أ] أحدها أن يتجزّى أن تكون القسمة داخلة في الماهية أعني أن تكون بفصول ذاتية في الأنواع؛ ويجب أن يستعان في هذا الباب؛ فالمواضع التي تذكر في الحجج الجدلية حيث تذكر مواضع هل الشيء جنس أو فصل أو ليس ؟ ويؤخذ من ذلك ما ليس مبنا على المشهورات الساذجة؛ ويستعان أيضًا بالمواضع التي يدل على أن الشيء عرض غير مقوم لماهية الشيء ليتحرر عن أن تكون القسمة بفصول عرضية. [ب] والثاني أن يستعان من القسمة الترتيب فيما هو في ترتيب القسمة أولي يجعل في ترتيب الحد أولا؛ وإن لم يكن أحدهما أولي بالنسبة
It indicates what is more general and what is more specific, so from this is derived the method of composing the parts of the definition, making the more general first and the more specific second. For example, in defining man, one says 'animal with two legs' — not 'not without two legs is animal' — for there is a difference between the two because 'animal' is repeated in the second, and 'with two legs' was an animal; not so in the first. [B] The second is that division indicates establishing each differentia with a genus above it — a genus for what is under it — so the differentiae are arranged in succession so that what is combined from the differentiae is combined in their succession; nothing of them is lost in the middle. When one wants to compose the definition from species up to genera, one does not leap from a species to a distant genus but to the genus immediately following it. [T] The third is that if division is fulfilled as required, it includes all the essential differentiae, so nothing of them remains, and thus the differentiae are given in their succession vertically; and also horizontally, for it is possible to divide a genus by two divisions one of which is not under the other, such as dividing an animate body into voluntary-mover and non-voluntary-mover, and into sentient and non-sentient at once; so one must observe this in division horizontally as one must vertically, lest a differentia be missed from among the differentiae — dividing into essential differentiae that are overlapping or coinciding. Overlapping like mortal and immortal, and rational and non-rational; coinciding like sentient and non-sentient, and voluntary-mover and non-voluntary-mover.
The law for observing the second and third aspects is that the division be by the essential constituents of the species, and that the division be a primary division of the genus — which is the division that belongs to the genus qua genus. For example, one must first divide animal into flying, swimming, creeping, and walking; then divide walking into two-legged and many-legged, and flying into connected-wing and separated-wing. If one violates this and first divides animal into connected-wing and separated-wing, then one has not divided animal as animal but as flying. Likewise, if one divides animal into many-legged and two-legged, one has not divided it as animal but as walking. So one must consider whether the genus needs an additional nature beyond generic nature to accept this division, or not; rather this division is primary for it. So one gives precedence to the division that is primary, and delays the division that is not primary. Then one makes a primary division of all the divided and the differentia; then another primary division, and so on until reaching what is only divisible by number. In summary, the differentiae must be essential in the division; the exposition of how that division is made has passed, and it is not necessary that every one of them be known.
And it was said in the First Teaching: not every divider is compelled in his division, nor the definer in his definition, to know everything, as some thought; rather one must observe in the division useful for definition three symptoms: [A] First: that the division be included in the quiddity — I mean that it be by essential differentiae in the species; and one must seek aid in this matter from the topics mentioned in dialectical arguments where topics are mentioned such as 'Is the thing a genus or a differentia or not?' And one takes from that what is not based on naive common opinions; and one also seeks aid from topics that indicate that a thing is an accident non-constitutive of the quiddity of the thing, to free oneself from the division being by accidental differentiae. [B] Second: that one seeks aid from division for the order: whatever is prior in the order of division is made prior in the order of the definition; even if neither of the two is prior in relation...
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is a methodological exposition on the rules of division (qisma) as a tool for composing correct definitions (hadd). The author explains three benefits of division for definition, then lays down a law for proper division, and finally lists three conditions for a division to be useful in definition.

First, the author describes three ways division aids definition: [أ] Division shows what is more general (a'amm) and what is more specific (akhass), so that in defining we place the genus first and the differentia second. For example, to define 'man' one says 'animal with two legs', not 'two-legged animal' because that would repeat 'animal' incorrectly. [ب] Division ensures each differentia is paired with its immediate genus, so the differentiae are arranged in a proper sequence without skipping levels. When composing a definition, one does not leap from a species to a distant genus but to the next higher genus. [ت] A complete division captures all essential differentiae in order—both vertically (along a single line) and horizontally (across coordinate divisions). The author gives the example of dividing 'animate body' into voluntary/non-voluntary movers and sentient/non-sentient. One must observe both vertical and horizontal divisions to avoid missing a differentia. Overlapping differentiae (e.g., mortal/immortal and rational/non-rational) and coinciding differentiae (e.g., sentient/non-sentient and voluntary/non-voluntary) are distinguished.

Next, the author states the law (qanun) for achieving the second and third aspects: the division must be by essential (dhati) constituents that constitute the species, and it must be a primary division of the genus—i.e., division qua genus. For instance, one must first divide 'animal' into flying, swimming, creeping, walking; then subdivide walking into two-legged/many-legged, and flying into connected/separated wings. If one divides 'animal' directly into connected/separated wings, that is a division of 'animal' as 'flying', not as 'animal'. The proper order is to apply primary divisions stepwise until reaching indivisible individuals (by number).

Finally, the author cites the 'First Teaching' (likely Aristotle's Topics) to note that neither the divider nor the definer needs to know everything; rather they must observe three symptoms (a'rad) in a useful division: [أ] The division must be internal to the quiddity (mahiyya), i.e., by essential differentiae of the species. One can consult dialectical topics (al-mawadi' al-jadaliyya) to determine whether something is a genus, differentia, or accident. [ب] The division provides an ordering principle: what is prior in the order of division should be placed first in the definition. The text cuts off before the third symptom is fully expounded.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that division must be by essential (not accidental) differentiae, and that the order must follow the natural hierarchy of genera and species.

intermediate
6 min
The Law of Primary Division (Qisma Awwaliyya)
Author explains the law of primary division for properly ordering differentiae.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the law of primary division and apply it to determine the correct order of divisions when defining a species.

Core Idea
Primary division divides a genus qua genus, avoiding subordination to an accidental nature.

The author lays down a law (qanun) for correct division: it must be by essential constituents and must be primary for the genus. This ensures that when we divide, we do not accidentally impose a nature that is not inherent to the genus. Let's explore the example of dividing 'animal'.

Guided Path
1
Understand the law of primary division
Division must be by entire essential constituents (dhatiyyat muqawwima) and must be primary division (qisma awwaliyya). Primary division means dividing the genus qua genus, not through an added nature.
2
Study the example of dividing animal
The author gives the correct order: first divide animal into flying, swimming, creeping, walking. Then subdivide walking into two-legged and many-legged, and flying into connected-wing and separated-wing.
3
Identify incorrect divisions
If one divides animal directly into connected-wing and separated-wing, that is a division of animal qua flying, not qua animal. Similarly, dividing animal into two-legged and many-legged is a division of animal qua walking.
4
Apply the test of additional nature
Check whether the genus needs an additional nature (tabi'a za'ida) to accept the division. If so, the division is not primary and should be deferred.
5
Continue stepwise until individuals
After each primary division, proceed to the next level until reaching what is only divisible by number (i.e., individuals). This ensures complete hierarchical coverage.

Source Text

يدل على ما هو أعم وعلى ما هو أخص فيستنبط من هذا كيفية تركيب أجزاء الحد فيجعل الأعم أولا والأخص ثانيًا. فيقال مثلا في تحديد الإنسان حيوان ذو رجلين «أ» ليس لا ذو رجلين حيوان ( أ ) ليس: فإن بين الأمرين فرقًا لما أن الحيوان في الثاني مكرّر؛ وقد كان ذو رجلين حيوانا؛ ولا كذلك في الأول. [ب] والثاني أن القسمة يدل على تقرير كل فصل مع جنس فوقه جنسا لما تحته فجرى ترتيب الفصول على التوالي حتى يكون ما يجتمع من الفصول إنما يجتمع على تواليها؛ فلا يذهب منها شيء في الوسط. فإذا أريد أن يركب الحد من الأنواع إلى الأجناس لم يظفر من نوع إلى جنس أبعد بل الجنس الذي يليه . [ت] والثالث أنها إذا وفيت على الواجب كانت تشتمل على الفصول الذاتية كلها فلا يبقى شيء منها فيكون قد أعطيت الفصول على تواليها طولا؛ ولو عرضًا فإنه يمكن أن يقسم الجنس بقسمين ليس أحدهما تحت الآخر مثل الجسم ذي النفس إلى المتحرك بالإرادة وغير المتحرك بالإرادة، وإلى الحسّاس وغير الحسّاس مرة؛ فيجب أن يكون مراعيًا لهذا في القسمة عرضًا كما يجب طولا كيلا يفوت فصل من فصول يقسم إلى فصول ذاتية متداخلة أو متوافقة. والمتداخلة مثل المائت وغير المائت، والناطق وغير الناطق المتوافقة مثل الحسّاس وغير الحسّاس، والمتحرك بالإرادة وغير المتحرك بالإرادة.
والقانون في مراعاة الوجه الثاني والثالث هو أن تكون القسمة بالذاتيات المقومات للأنواع، وأن تكون القسمة قسمة أولية للجنس وهي القسمة التي يكون للجنس في القسمة التي للجنس من طريق ما هو جنس مثلا يجب أن يقسم الحيوان أولا إلى الطائر والسابح والزاحف والماشي: ثم يقسم الماشي إلى ذي رجلين وذي الأرجل، والطائر إلى متصل الجناح ومنفصل الجناح. فإن أحل بهذا وقسم الحيوان أولا إلى متصل الجناح ومنفصل الجناح فما قسم الحيوان من جهة ما هو حيوان بل من جهة ما هو طائر. وكذلك إذا قسم الحيوان إلى ذي الأرجل وذي رجلين فإنه ما قسّم من جهة ما هو حيوان بل من جهة ما هو ماشي فيجب أن ينظر هل يحتاج الجنس / إلى أن تصير له [٣١٦] طبيعة زائدة على طبيعة الجنسية حتى تقبل هذه القسمة، أو لا يحتاج بل وهذه القسمة له أولا؛ فتقدم القسمة التي تكون أولا، وتؤخّر القسمة التي لا تكون أولا . فإذا قسم قسمة أولية جميع المقسوم والفصل؛ ثم قسم قسمة أولية أخرى. وكذلك إلى أن ينتهي إلى ما لا ينقسم إلا بالعدد. وبالجملة يجب أن تكون الفصول ذاتية في القسمة؛ وبيان كيفية تلك القسمة قد مرَّ، ولا يلزم أن يكون واحد منها معلومًا.
وقد قيل في التعليم الأول لا كل المنقسم يضطر في تقسيمه، ولا المحدد في تحديده إلى أن يعلم كل شيء على ما ظن بعضهم بل يلزم أن يراعي في القسمة النافعة في التحديد أعراضًا ثلاثة [أ] أحدها أن يتجزّى أن تكون القسمة داخلة في الماهية أعني أن تكون بفصول ذاتية في الأنواع؛ ويجب أن يستعان في هذا الباب؛ فالمواضع التي تذكر في الحجج الجدلية حيث تذكر مواضع هل الشيء جنس أو فصل أو ليس ؟ ويؤخذ من ذلك ما ليس مبنا على المشهورات الساذجة؛ ويستعان أيضًا بالمواضع التي يدل على أن الشيء عرض غير مقوم لماهية الشيء ليتحرر عن أن تكون القسمة بفصول عرضية. [ب] والثاني أن يستعان من القسمة الترتيب فيما هو في ترتيب القسمة أولي يجعل في ترتيب الحد أولا؛ وإن لم يكن أحدهما أولي بالنسبة
It indicates what is more general and what is more specific, so from this is derived the method of composing the parts of the definition, making the more general first and the more specific second. Division Must Be by Essential Differentiae
Author criticizes improper divisions and states the first condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify improper divisions in definition and correct them by ensuring the differentia is essential to the genus.

Core Idea
Division for definition must cut at the joints of essence, not of accident.

The author begins by showing how a division can go wrong: dividing 'animal' into 'connected-wing' and 'separated-wing' treats it as if it were a bird. Similarly, dividing it into quadrupeds and bipeds treats it as a walker. These divisions miss what makes an animal an animal. The first requirement for a definitional division is that it uses essential differentiate that belong to the thing's nature. This lesson unpacks that requirement and shows how to avoid accidental divisions.

Guided Path
1
Find the improper division
Locate the examples in the Arabic where the author criticizes dividing 'animal' into 'connected-wing/separated-wing' and 'quadrupeds/bipeds'. What is the problem?
The first divides animal as bird, the second as walker—neither is essential to animality.
2
Extract the principle
The author states: division must be by essential differentiate (فصول ذاتية) that enter into the essence (داخلة في الماهية). This is the first condition for a useful division in definition.
3
Apply to a new case
Consider defining 'salat' as a species of 'ibadah'. An improper division would be dividing 'ibadah' into 'salat' and 'du'a' (supplication) based on the accidental property of being ritual vs. informal. But the essential differentia for salat is its specific form (ruku', sujud, etc.).
Use an Islamic example from fiqh.

Source Text

إلى ذي رجلين وذي الأرجل، والطائر إلى متصل الجناح ومنفصل الجناح. فإن أحل بهذا وقسم الحيوان أولا إلى متصل الجناح ومنفصل الجناح فما قسم الحيوان من جهة ما هو حيوان بل من جهة ما هو طائر. وكذلك إذا قسم الحيوان إلى ذي الأرجل وذي رجلين فإنه ما قسّم من جهة ما هو حيوان بل من جهة ما هو ماشي فيجب أن ينظر هل يحتاج الجنس / إلى أن تصير له [٣١٦] طبيعة زائدة على طبيعة الجنسية حتى تقبل هذه القسمة، أو لا يحتاج بل وهذه القسمة له أولا؛ فتقدم القسمة التي تكون أولا، وتؤخّر القسمة التي لا تكون أولا . فإذا قسم قسمة أولية جميع المقسوم والفصل؛ ثم قسم قسمة أولية أخرى. وكذلك إلى أن ينتهي إلى ما لا ينقسم إلا بالعدد. وبالجملة يجب أن تكون الفصول ذاتية في القسمة؛ وبيان كيفية تلك القسمة قد مرَّ، ولا يلزم أن يكون واحد منها معلومًا.
وقد قيل في التعليم الأول لا كل المنقسم يضطر في تقسيمه، ولا المحدد في تحديده إلى أن يعلم كل شيء على ما ظن بعضهم بل يلزم أن يراعي في القسمة النافعة في التحديد أعراضًا ثلاثة [أ] أحدها أن يتجزّى أن تكون القسمة داخلة في الماهية أعني أن تكون بفصول ذاتية في الأنواع؛ ويجب أن يستعان في هذا الباب؛ فالمواضع التي تذكر في الحجج الجدلية حيث تذكر مواضع هل الشيء جنس أو فصل أو ليس ؟ ويؤخذ من ذلك ما ليس مبنا على المشهورات الساذجة؛ ويستعان أيضًا بالمواضع التي يدل على أن الشيء عرض غير مقوم لماهية الشيء ليتحرر عن أن تكون القسمة بفصول عرضية. [ب] والثاني أن يستعان من القسمة الترتيب فيما هو في ترتيب القسمة أولي يجعل في ترتيب الحد أولا؛ وإن لم يكن أحدهما أولي بالنسبة إلى الآخر يقوم ما هو أشبه بالمادة دون ما هو أشبه بالغائية؛ إذ ذاك لا يؤخّر. وإن لم يختلفا يقوم أحدهما على الآخر إما هذا وإما ذلك. [ت] والثالث أن لا يزال يقسم حتى يبلغ الشيء المحدود إن كان نوعا متوسطا، أو ينتهي إلى آخر القسمة التي بالذاتيات التي ليس بعدها إلا أن القسمة بالعرضيات إن كُنتَ تريد تحديد الأنواع الأخيرة. ثم قيل إنك إذا أحضرت بالقسمة مثلا جميع المحمولات الداخلة في ما هو مميز المشتركات منها المتشابهة في أنواع كثيرة، ومميز الخواص بنوع نوع ليحد الجنس فترتبه أولا ؛ ثم أردفه بالفصول. فإن وقع في بدل شيء مقول على كثيرين؛ وطلب المحمولات الخاصة التي لواحد واحد من الكثيرين من جهة ذلك فيركب الحد، ثم رفعت ما يخصُّ واحدا واحدا فلم يبقَ شيء من المعنى مشتركا. وبالجملة يلزم أن تؤخذ محمولات الشيء من جهة ذلك الشيء نوعا كان ذلك الشيء أو جنســا؛ إذ المقصود معرفة الجنس والفصل لذلك الشيء. فإذا عرف الفصل أو لا يطلب الجنس ليقدم عليه، وإذا عرف الجنس أولا يطلب الفصل ليؤخّر عنه، فإن المركَّب من الجنس والفصل هو الحد على ما عرف. واعلم بأنه كما يمكن أن يبتدأ في التحديد من الكليات فكذلك يمكن أن يبتدأ من الجزئيات؛ والأمر على الغلط بسبب اشتراك الاسم الخفي في هذا وهو أن يبتدأ من الجزئيات أقل. وكما أن الغرض المقدم في القياس هو أن يكون مظهر التصديق الخفي فكذلك يجب أن يكون الغرض المقدم في الحدود هو أن يكون مظهر التصور الخفي؛ والشيء لا يكون مظهرًا للشيء إلا وأن يكون في غاية الظهور وإلا لا يظهر الخفي منه، وهذا ظاهر (۱).
To the two-legged and the quadrupeds, and the bird to the connected-wing and separated-wing. For if one does this and divides animal first into connected-wing and separated-wing, then he did not divide animal insofar as it is animal but insofar as it is a bird. Likewise, if he divides animal into quadrupeds and bipeds, then he did not divide it insofar as it is animal but insofar as it is a walker. So it must be considered whether the genus needs an additional nature beyond the generic nature to accept this division, or does not need but rather this division is primary for it. So the division that is primary is presented first, and the division that is not primary is delayed. So he divides with a primary division the whole of the divided and the differentia; then he divides with another primary division. And so on until he reaches what is not divisible except by number. In summary, the differentiae must be essential in the division; the explanation of how that division is done has passed, and it is not necessary that one of them be known. And it has been said in the First Teaching: Not every divided thing compels in its division, nor the definer in his definition, to know everything as some thought, but rather it is necessary to observe in the useful division for definition three accidents [conditions]: [a] The first is that the division is to be taken as entering into the essence, meaning that it be by essential differentiae in the species; and one must seek aid in this matter from the places mentioned in dialectical arguments where the places are mentioned of whether a thing is a genus or a differentia or not; and one takes from that what is not based on naive commonplaces; and one also seeks aid from the places that indicate that a thing is an accident not constitutive of the essence of a thing to free it from the division being by accidental differentiae. [b] The second is that one uses from the division the order: what is prior in the order of division is made first in the order of the definition; and if one of them is not prior with respect to the other, what is more like matter is placed before what is more like finality; since that [final] is not delayed. And if they do not differ, one of them is placed before the other, either this or that. [c] The third is that one continues dividing until reaching the defined thing if it is a middle species, or until ending at the last division by essential properties after which there is nothing except division by accidentals if you intend to define the ultimate species. Then it is said that if you bring by division, for example, all the predicates entering into the whatness distinguishing the common ones that are similar in many species and distinguishing the properties species by species to define the genus, you arrange it first; then you follow it with the differentiae. If something happens in place of something predicated of many, you seek the special predicates that belong to each one of the many insofar as that, then you compose the definition, then you remove what is specific to one by one, so nothing of the meaning remains common. In summary, it is necessary to take the predicates of a thing insofar as that thing, whether that thing is a species or a genus; for the purpose is to know the genus and differentia of that thing. So if the differentia is known, the genus is sought to precede it; and if the genus is known first, the differentia is sought to follow it; for the composite of genus and differentia is the definition as has been known. And know that just as it is possible to begin defining from universals, so too it is possible to begin from particulars; and the matter is erroneous due to the hidden homonymy in this, which is that beginning from particulars is less. And just as the primary purpose in syllogism is to be a revealer of hidden assent, so too the primary purpose in definitions must be to be a revealer of hidden conception; and a thing is not a revealer of another thing unless it is in the utmost clarity, otherwise the hidden from it does not become manifest, and this is evident. (1)
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage discusses the proper method of division (qisma) when constructing a definition (hadd). The author begins by critiquing an improper division: if you divide 'animal' into 'connected-wing' and 'separated-wing', you are dividing it not as animal but as bird; similarly, dividing animal into quadrupeds and bipeds divides it as a walker, not as animal. The point is that division must be by essential differentiate (fusul dhatiyya) that pertain to the essence of the thing being divided. The author then raises a question: does the genus need an additional nature beyond its generic nature to accept such division? The answer, implicit, is that the division should be primary—i.e., the first division of the genus should be by its immediate differentiae. The author emphasizes that the differentiae in division must be essential. He then cites the 'First Teaching' (likely Aristotle's Topics) to set forth three conditions (a'rad) for a division to be useful in definition:

[a] The division must enter into the essence, meaning that it uses essential differentiae that constitute the species. To ensure this, one should consult dialectical loci that determine whether something is genus, differentia, or accident, avoiding naive commonplaces.

[b] The order of division should be reflected in the order of the definition: what is prior in division is placed first in the definition. If neither is prior, place what is more like matter before what is more like finality (gha'iyya); if they do not differ, either order is acceptable.

[c] One must continue dividing until reaching the defined thing—if it is a middle species, stop at its immediate genus and differentia; if it is an ultimate species, continue down to the last essential division, after which only accidental divisions remain.

The author then describes the practical process: gather all predicates that enter into the essence, distinguish the common (shared by many species) and the proper (specific to each species), arrange the genus first, then append the differentiae. If a predicate applies to many, seek the specific predicates belonging to each one, compose the definition, then remove what is specific to single individuals so that no meaning remains common. The goal is to know the genus and differentia of the thing. If you know the differentia first, seek the genus to precede it; if you know the genus first, seek the differentia to follow it, because the definition is composed of genus and differentia.

Finally, the author notes that one can begin defining from universals or from particulars, but starting from particulars is less common and can be erroneous due to hidden homonymy. Just as the purpose of syllogism is to reveal hidden assent (tasdiq), the purpose of definition is to reveal hidden conception (tasawwur). A thing can only reveal something else if it is itself very clear; otherwise, the hidden does not become manifest.

جنس
قسمة
حد

According to the passage, why is dividing 'animal' into 'connected-wing' and 'separated-wing' improper?
A) Because it divides by an essential differentia.
B) Because it divides animal as bird, not as animal.
C) Because it uses too many differentiate.
D) Because it is not primary.

Key Takeaway
Dividing a genus for definition must use essential differentiate that belong to the essence of the thing, not accidental properties.

?

The Three Conditions for Useful Division in Definition
Author enumerates three conditions for useful division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate and explain the three conditions for division to be useful in definition, and evaluate a given division against them.

Core Idea
Useful division in definition requires essence penetration, correct order, and exhaustive coverage.

The author lists three 'accidents' (conditions) that a division must satisfy to be useful for definition. The first ensures the differentiate are essential. The second ensures the order in the division is reflected in the definition, prioritizing matter-like over form-like. The third ensures the division continues until the defined thing is reached. These are practical rules for constructing definitions that reveal essences.

Guided Path
1
List the three conditions
Identify the three conditions marked as [a], [b], [c] in the Arabic text. They begin with 'أحدها', 'والثاني', 'والثالث'.
2
Explain each condition
Condition 1: Division must enter into the essence, i.e., use essential differentiate. Condition 2: The order of division determines the order in the definition: what is prior in division is first in definition; between matter-like and form-like, place matter first. Condition 3: Continue dividing until you reach the defined item (if middle species, stop at immediate genus; if ultimate species, go to last essential division).
Use the author's examples if available.
3
Apply to an example
Define 'salat' as a species of 'ibadah'. Check condition 1: differentia (e.g., 'having specific pillars') is essential. Condition 2: 'Ibadah' is genus, 'salat' is species; order is correct. Condition 3: Continue until 'salat' is reached—if it's an ultimate species (yes), then no further division by essentials needed.

إلى ذي رجلين وذي الأرجل، والطائر إلى متصل الجناح ومنفصل الجناح. فإن أحل بهذا وقسم الحيوان أولا إلى متصل الجناح ومنفصل الجناح فما قسم الحيوان من جهة ما هو حيوان بل من جهة ما هو طائر. وكذلك إذا قسم الحيوان إلى ذي الأرجل وذي رجلين فإنه ما قسّم من جهة ما هو حيوان بل من جهة ما هو ماشي فيجب أن ينظر هل يحتاج الجنس / إلى أن تصير له [٣١٦] طبيعة زائدة على طبيعة الجنسية حتى تقبل هذه القسمة، أو لا يحتاج بل وهذه القسمة له أولا؛ فتقدم القسمة التي تكون أولا، وتؤخّر القسمة التي لا تكون أولا . فإذا قسم قسمة أولية جميع المقسوم والفصل؛ ثم قسم قسمة أولية أخرى. وكذلك إلى أن ينتهي إلى ما لا ينقسم إلا بالعدد. وبالجملة يجب أن تكون الفصول ذاتية في القسمة؛ وبيان كيفية تلك القسمة قد مرَّ، ولا يلزم أن يكون واحد منها معلومًا.

[ب] والثاني أن يستعان من القسمة الترتيب فيما هو في ترتيب القسمة أولي يجعل في ترتيب الحد أولا؛ وإن لم يكن أحدهما أولي بالنسبة إلى الآخر يقوم ما هو أشبه بالمادة دون ما هو أشبه بالغائية؛ إذ ذاك لا يؤخّر. وإن لم يختلفا يقوم أحدهما على الآخر إما هذا وإما ذلك. [ت] والثالث أن لا يزال يقسم حتى يبلغ الشيء المحدود إن كان نوعا متوسطا، أو ينتهي إلى آخر القسمة التي بالذاتيات التي ليس بعدها إلا أن القسمة بالعرضيات إن كُنتَ تريد تحديد الأنواع الأخيرة. ثم قيل إنك إذا أحضرت بالقسمة مثلا جميع المحمولات الداخلة في ما هو مميز المشتركات منها المتشابهة في أنواع كثيرة، ومميز الخواص بنوع نوع ليحد الجنس فترتبه أولا ؛ ثم أردفه بالفصول. فإن وقع في بدل شيء مقول على كثيرين؛ وطلب المحمولات الخاصة التي لواحد واحد من الكثيرين من جهة ذلك فيركب الحد، ثم رفعت ما يخصُّ واحدا واحدا فلم يبقَ شيء من المعنى مشتركا. وبالجملة يلزم أن تؤخذ محمولات الشيء من جهة ذلك الشيء نوعا كان ذلك الشيء أو جنســا؛ إذ المقصود معرفة الجنس والفصل لذلك الشيء. فإذا عرف الفصل أو لا يطلب الجنس ليقدم عليه، وإذا عرف الجنس أولا يطلب الفصل ليؤخّر عنه، فإن المركَّب من الجنس والفصل هو الحد على ما عرف. واعلم بأنه كما يمكن أن يبتدأ في التحديد من الكليات فكذلك يمكن أن يبتدأ من الجزئيات؛ والأمر على الغلط بسبب اشتراك الاسم الخفي في هذا وهو أن يبتدأ من الجزئيات أقل. وكما أن الغرض المقدم في القياس هو أن يكون مظهر التصديق الخفي فكذلك يجب أن يكون الغرض المقدم في الحدود هو أن يكون مظهر التصور الخفي؛ والشيء لا يكون مظهرًا للشيء إلا وأن يكون في غاية الظهور وإلا لا يظهر الخفي منه، وهذا ظاهر (۱).

Constructing a Definition by Division
Author describes the practical method of constructing a definition by division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a definition by gathering essential predicates, ordering genus before differentia, and removing individual specifics.

Core Idea
Definition by division is like carving: collect all essential predicates, identify the common genus, then add differentiate that distinguish each species, removing what is particular to individuals.

After laying down the conditions, the author describes the practical process of constructing a definition by division. You collect all predicates that enter into the essence of the thing, distinguish those shared among many species from those unique to each, arrange the genus first, then append the differentiate. Then you remove any predicates that apply only to individual instances, leaving only what is common to all members of the species. This yields a definition that captures the essence.

Guided Path
1
Gather all essential predicates
List all predicates (محمولات) that enter into the whatness (ماهية) of the thing you want to define. In the text, 'all the predicates entering into the whatness' are to be brought by division.
Example: For 'salat', predicates include: 'ibadah', 'with ruku' and sujud', 'with takbir', 'with specific recitations', etc.
2
Distinguish common from proper
Identify which predicates are shared by many species (common) and which are specific to one species (proper). The common ones will form the genus; the proper ones will form the differentia.
'Ibadah' is common to salat, sawm, zakat, etc. 'With ruku' and sujud' is proper to salat.
3
Order and compose the definition
Place the genus first, then the differentia. The text says: 'arrange it first; then follow it with the differentiae' (ترتبه أولا ثم أردفه بالفصول). This yields the definition: genus + differentia.
If you know the differentia first, seek the genus to precede it.
4
Remove individual specifics
Remove any predicates that apply only to individual instances (e.g., 'the salat of Zaid'). The definition should only contain what is common to all members of the species.
'then you remove what is specific to one by one, so nothing of the meaning remains common.'

إلى ذي رجلين وذي الأرجل، والطائر إلى متصل الجناح ومنفصل الجناح. فإن أحل بهذا وقسم الحيوان أولا إلى متصل الجناح ومنفصل الجناح فما قسم الحيوان من جهة ما هو حيوان بل من جهة ما هو طائر. وكذلك إذا قسم الحيوان إلى ذي الأرجل وذي رجلين فإنه ما قسّم من جهة ما هو حيوان بل من جهة ما هو ماشي فيجب أن ينظر هل يحتاج الجنس / إلى أن تصير له [٣١٦] طبيعة زائدة على طبيعة الجنسية حتى تقبل هذه القسمة، أو لا يحتاج بل وهذه القسمة له أولا؛ فتقدم القسمة التي تكون أولا، وتؤخّر القسمة التي لا تكون أولا . فإذا قسم قسمة أولية جميع المقسوم والفصل؛ ثم قسم قسمة أولية أخرى. وكذلك إلى أن ينتهي إلى ما لا ينقسم إلا بالعدد. وبالجملة يجب أن تكون الفصول ذاتية في القسمة؛ وبيان كيفية تلك القسمة قد مرَّ، ولا يلزم أن يكون واحد منها معلومًا.
وقد قيل في التعليم الأول لا كل المنقسم يضطر في تقسيمه، ولا المحدد في تحديده إلى أن يعلم كل شيء على ما ظن بعضهم بل يلزم أن يراعي في القسمة النافعة في التحديد أعراضًا ثلاثة [أ] أحدها أن يتجزّى أن تكون القسمة داخلة في الماهية أعني أن تكون بفصول ذاتية في الأنواع؛ ويجب أن يستعان في هذا الباب؛ فالمواضع التي تذكر في الحجج الجدلية حيث تذكر مواضع هل الشيء جنس أو فصل أو ليس ؟ ويؤخذ من ذلك ما ليس مبنا على المشهورات الساذجة؛ ويستعان أيضًا بالمواضع التي يدل على أن الشيء عرض غير مقوم لماهية الشيء ليتحرر عن أن تكون القسمة بفصول عرضية. [ب] والثاني أن يستعان من القسمة الترتيب فيما هو في ترتيب القسمة أولي يجعل في ترتيب الحد أولا؛ وإن لم يكن أحدهما أولي بالنسبة إلى الآخر يقوم ما هو أشبه بالمادة دون ما هو أشبه بالغائية؛ إذ ذاك لا يؤخّر. وإن لم يختلفا يقوم أحدهما على الآخر إما هذا وإما ذلك. [ت] والثالث أن لا يزال يقسم حتى يبلغ الشيء المحدود إن كان نوعا متوسطا، أو ينتهي إلى آخر القسمة التي بالذاتيات التي ليس بعدها إلا أن القسمة بالعرضيات إن كُنتَ تريد تحديد الأنواع الأخيرة. ثم قيل إنك إذا أحضرت بالقسمة مثلا جميع المحمولات الداخلة في ما هو مميز المشتركات منها المتشابهة في أنواع كثيرة، ومميز الخواص بنوع نوع ليحد الجنس فترتبه أولا ؛ ثم أردفه بالفصول. فإن وقع في بدل شيء مقول على كثيرين؛ وطلب المحمولات الخاصة التي لواحد واحد من الكثيرين من جهة ذلك فيركب الحد، ثم رفعت ما يخصُّ واحدا واحدا فلم يبقَ شيء من المعنى مشتركا. وبالجملة يلزم أن تؤخذ محمولات الشيء من جهة ذلك الشيء نوعا كان ذلك الشيء أو جنســا؛ إذ المقصود معرفة الجنس والفصل لذلك الشيء. فإذا عرف الفصل أو لا يطلب الجنس ليقدم عليه، وإذا عرف الجنس أولا يطلب الفصل ليؤخّر عنه، فإن المركَّب من الجنس والفصل هو الحد على ما عرف. واعلم بأنه كما يمكن أن يبتدأ في التحديد من الكليات فكذلك يمكن أن يبتدأ من الجزئيات؛ والأمر على الغلط بسبب اشتراك الاسم الخفي في هذا وهو أن يبتدأ من الجزئيات أقل. وكما أن الغرض المقدم في القياس هو أن يكون مظهر التصديق الخفي فكذلك يجب أن يكون الغرض المقدم في الحدود هو أن يكون مظهر التصور الخفي؛ والشيء لا يكون مظهرًا للشيء إلا وأن يكون في غاية الظهور وإلا لا يظهر الخفي منه، وهذا ظاهر (۱).
To the two-legged and the quadrupeds, and the bird to the connected-wing and separated-wing. For if one does this and divides animal first into connected-wing and separated-wing, then he did not divide animal insofar as it is animal but insofar as it is a bird. Likewise, if he divides animal into quadrupeds and bipeds, then he did not divide it insofar as it is animal but insofar as it is a walker. So it must be considered whether the genus needs an additional nature beyond the generic nature to accept this division, or does not need but rather this division is primary for it. So the division that is primary is presented first, and the division that is not primary is delayed. So he divides with a primary division the whole of the divided and the differentia; then he divides with another primary division. And so on until he reaches what is not divisible except by number. In summary, the differentiae must be essential in the division; the explanation of how that division is done has passed, and it is not necessary that one of them be known. And it has been said in the First Teaching: Not every divided thing compels in its division, nor the definer in his definition, to know everything as some thought, but rather it is necessary to observe in the useful division for definition three accidents [conditions]: [a] The first is that the division is to be taken as entering into the essence, meaning that it be by essential differentiae in the species; and one must seek aid in this matter from the places mentioned in dialectical arguments where the places are mentioned of whether a thing is a genus or a differentia or not; and one takes from that what is not based on naive commonplaces; and one also seeks aid from the places that indicate that a thing is an accident not constitutive of the essence of a thing to free it from the division being by accidental differentiae. [b] The second is that one uses from the division the order: what is prior in the order of division is made first in the order of the definition; and if one of them is not prior with respect to the other, what is more like matter is placed before what is more like finality; since that [final] is not delayed. And if they do not differ, one of them is placed before the other, either this or that. [c] The third is that one continues dividing until reaching the defined thing if it is a middle species, or until ending at the last division by essential properties after which there is nothing except division by accidentals if you intend to define the ultimate species. Then it is said that if you bring by division, for example, all the predicates entering into the whatness distinguishing the common ones that are similar in many species and distinguishing the properties species by species to define the genus, you arrange it first; then you follow it with the differentiae. If something happens in place of something predicated of many, you seek the special predicates that belong to each one of the many insofar as that, then you compose the definition, then you remove what is specific to one by one, so nothing of the meaning remains common. In summary, it is necessary to take the predicates of a thing insofar as that thing, whether that thing is a species or a genus; for the purpose is to know the genus and differentia of that thing. So if the differentia is known, the genus is sought to precede it; and if the genus is known first, the differentia is sought to follow it; for the composite of genus and differentia is the definition as has been known. And know that just as it is possible to begin defining from universals, so too it is possible to begin from particulars; and the matter is erroneous due to the hidden homonymy in this, which is that beginning from particulars is less. And just as the primary purpose in syllogism is to be a revealer of hidden assent, so too the primary purpose in definitions must be to be a revealer of hidden conception; and a thing is not a revealer of another thing unless it is in the utmost clarity, otherwise the hidden from it does not become manifest, and this is evident. (1)
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage discusses the proper method of division (qisma) when constructing a definition (hadd). The author begins by critiquing an improper division: if you divide 'animal' into 'connected-wing' and 'separated-wing', you are dividing it not as animal but as bird; similarly, dividing animal into quadrupeds and bipeds divides it as a walker, not as animal. The point is that division must be by essential differentiate (fusul dhatiyya) that pertain to the essence of the thing being divided. The author then raises a question: does the genus need an additional nature beyond its generic nature to accept such division? The answer, implicit, is that the division should be primary—i.e., the first division of the genus should be by its immediate differentiae. The author emphasizes that the differentiae in division must be essential. He then cites the 'First Teaching' (likely Aristotle's Topics) to set forth three conditions (a'rad) for a division to be useful in definition:

[a] The division must enter into the essence, meaning that it uses essential differentiae that constitute the species. To ensure this, one should consult dialectical loci that determine whether something is genus, differentia, or accident, avoiding naive commonplaces.

[b] The order of division should be reflected in the order of the definition: what is prior in division is placed first in the definition. If neither is prior, place what is more like matter before what is more like finality (gha'iyya); if they do not differ, either order is acceptable.

[c] One must continue dividing until reaching the defined thing—if it is a middle species, stop at its immediate genus and differentia; if it is an ultimate species, continue down to the last essential division, after which only accidental divisions remain.

The author then describes the practical process: gather all predicates that enter into the essence, distinguish the common (shared by many species) and the proper (specific to each species), arrange the genus first, then append the differentiae. If a predicate applies to many, seek the specific predicates belonging to each one, compose the definition, then remove what is specific to single individuals so that no meaning remains common. The goal is to know the genus and differentia of the thing. If you know the differentia first, seek the genus to precede it; if you know the genus first, seek the differentia to follow it, because the definition is composed of genus and differentia.

Finally, the author notes that one can begin defining from universals or from particulars, but starting from particulars is less common and can be erroneous due to hidden homonymy. Just as the purpose of syllogism is to reveal hidden assent (tasdiq), the purpose of definition is to reveal hidden conception (tasawwur). A thing can only reveal something else if it is itself very clear; otherwise, the hidden does not become manifest.

Key Terms
محمول
ماهية
جنس
فصل
حد

Checkpoint
What should you do after gathering all predicates and arranging the genus first?
A) Add the differentia immediately.
B) Remove predicates that are specific to individuals.
C) Seek the special predicates for each species.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
Definition by division requires collecting essential predicates, separating common from proper, ordering genus before differentia, and stripping away individual-specific content.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Apply the method to define 'iman' (faith) as a species of 'belief'. List essential predicates, distinguish common and proper, compose the definition, and remove individual specifics.
?
Take the definition of 'kalam nafsi' (internal speech) from kalam. Does it follow this method? Identify the genus and differentia.

The Purpose of Definition: Revealing Hidden Conceptions
Author concludes with the purpose of definition and its analogy to syllogism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the analogy between syllogism and definition, and why definitions must start from what is clearer.

Core Idea
Just as a syllogism reveals hidden assent, a definition reveals hidden conception by starting from what is more known.

The author ends the passage by drawing a parallel between syllogism (qiyas) and definition (hadd). The syllogism aims to make hidden assent (tasdiq) manifest by proceeding from clearer premises. Similarly, definition aims to make hidden conception (tasawwur) manifest by proceeding from what is clearer in the mind. This is why the components of a definition—genus and differentia—must be more evident than the thing being defined. The author also notes that one can start from universals or particulars, but starting from particulars is problematic due to hidden homonymy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the analogy
The author states: 'just as the primary purpose in syllogism is to be a revealer of hidden assent, so too the primary purpose in definitions must be to be a revealer of hidden conception'.
Syllogism reveals truth (tasdiq), definition reveals meaning (tasawwur).
2
Explain why clarity is needed
A thing can only reveal something else if it is itself in the utmost clarity (في غاية الظهور). Otherwise the hidden does not become manifest.
The genus and differentia must be better known than the defined term.
3
Apply to an Islamic example
To define 'tawhid', you might use 'belief that Allah is one with no partner'. The genus 'belief' is clearer than 'tawhid'? Possibly. But if you use advanced kalam terms, they may not be clearer. The definition fails if its components are not more known.
Check: Is 'belief' clearer than 'tawhid' for the average Muslim? Possibly, but for a theologian, maybe not.

Definition by Division: A Method for Constructing Hadd
Author explains definition by division method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of division (qisma) to construct a definition (hadd) by identifying genus and differentia in the correct order.

Core Idea
Definition by division reveals hidden conceptions by moving from clearer to hidden terms.

In this passage, the author explains a systematic method for constructing definitions through division (qisma). He emphasizes starting from what is more apparent and proceeding step by step until the defined thing is reached. This lesson will guide you through that process, showing how to arrange genera and differentiae to form a complete definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined concept
Determine what is being defined—whether it is a species or a genus. The method adapts accordingly; for an intermediate species, continue dividing until you reach it; for ultimate species, use essential properties.
The author distinguishes between dividing by essential properties and accidental properties, depending on the target.
2
Gather essential predicates
Collect all predicates that enter into the definition of the thing, distinguishing commonalities shared across many species and special properties unique to each species. Arrange them first by genus, then by differentiae.
If a predicate applies to many, seek the specific predicates for each, compose the definition, then remove what is particular so only the shared meaning remains.
3
Order genus and differentia
The genus must precede the differentia in the definition. If the differentia is known first, seek the genus to place it before; if the genus is known first, seek the differentia to follow. The definition is the composite of genus and differentia.
This ordering ensures clarity, as the genus provides the broader context and the differentia specifies the unique essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلى الآخر يقوم ما هو أشبه بالمادة دون ما هو أشبه بالغائية؛ إذ ذاك لا يؤخّر. وإن لم يختلفا يقوم أحدهما على الآخر إما هذا وإما ذلك. والثالث أن لا يزال يقسم حتى يبلغ الشيء المحدود إن كان نوعا متوسطا، أو ينتهي إلى آخر القسمة التي بالذاتيات التي ليس بعدها إلا أن القسمة بالعرضيات إن كُنتَ تريد تحديد الأنواع الأخيرة. ثم قيل إنك إذا أحضرت بالقسمة مثلا جميع المحمولات الداخلة في ما هو مميز المشتركات منها المتشابهة في أنواع كثيرة، ومميز الخواص بنوع نوع ليحد الجنس فترتبه أولا ؛ ثم أردفه بالفصول. فإن وقع في بدل شيء مقول على كثيرين؛ وطلب المحمولات الخاصة التي لواحد واحد من الكثيرين من جهة ذلك فيركب الحد، ثم رفعت ما يخصُّ واحدا واحدا فلم يبقَ شيء من المعنى مشتركا. وبالجملة يلزم أن تؤخذ محمولات الشيء من جهة ذلك الشيء نوعا كان ذلك الشيء أو جنســا؛ إذ المقصود معرفة الجنس والفصل لذلك الشيء. فإذا عرف الفصل أو لا يطلب الجنس ليقدم عليه، وإذا عرف الجنس أولا يطلب الفصل ليؤخّر عنه، فإن المركَّب من الجنس والفصل هو الحد على ما عرف. واعلم بأنه كما يمكن أن يبتدأ في التحديد من الكليات فكذلك يمكن أن يبتدأ من الجزئيات؛ والأمر على الغلط بسبب اشتراك الاسم الخفي في هذا وهو أن يبتدأ من الجزئيات أقل. وكما أن الغرض المقدم في القياس هو أن يكون مظهر التصديق الخفي فكذلك يجب أن يكون الغرض المقدم في الحدود هو أن يكون مظهر التصور الخفي؛ والشيء لا يكون مظهرًا للشيء إلا وأن يكون في غاية الظهور وإلا لا يظهر الخفي منه، وهذا ظاهر.
To the other stands what is more like matter rather than what is more like final cause; for then it is not delayed. And if they are not different, one of them stands over the other, either this or that. The third is that one continues dividing until one reaches the defined thing if it is an intermediate species, or until the end of the division by essential properties beyond which there is nothing except that division by accidental properties if you intend to define the ultimate species. Then it was said: When you bring, by division for example, all the predicates entering into what distinguishes the commonalities among them similar in many species, and distinguishes the properties by species by species to define the genus, then you arrange it first; then you follow it with the differentiae. And if it occurs in exchange of something said of many, and you seek the special predicates which are for each one of the many from that aspect, then you compose the definition, then you remove what is particular to each one, and nothing remains of the meaning shared. In summary, it is necessary to take the predicates of a thing from the aspect of that thing, whether that thing is a species or a genus; for the aim is to know the genus and differentia of that thing. So if the differentia is known first, one seeks the genus to precede it; and if the genus is known first, one seeks the differentia to follow it; for the composite of genus and differentia is the definition as known. And know that just as it is possible to begin in definition from universals, so too it is possible to begin from particulars; the matter is based on error due to the hidden homonymy in this: that one begins from fewer particulars. And just as the primary purpose in syllogism is to be a revealer of hidden assent, so too the primary purpose in definitions must be to be a revealer of hidden conception; and a thing is not a revealer of another thing unless it is in utmost clarity, otherwise the hidden does not become apparent from it, and this is evident.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage explains the method of definition by division (qisma). The author discusses the third mode of division: one continues dividing until reaching the defined thing (if it is an intermediate species) or until the division by essential properties ends, beyond which only accidental division remains if one aims to define ultimate species. The process involves gathering all predicates that distinguish commonalities and special properties, arranging the genus first, then adding differentiae. If a predicate applies to many, one seeks the specific predicates for each, composing the definition, then removing what is particular so that only the shared meaning remains. The key is to take predicates from the aspect of the thing itself, whether it is a species or genus, to know its genus and differentia. The order: if the differentia is known first, the genus is sought to precede it; if the genus is known first, the differentia is sought to follow it. The definition is the composite of genus and differentia. The author notes that one can start from universals or particulars in definition, but starting from particulars is less common and involves the error of hidden homonymy. Analogous to syllogism revealing hidden assent, definitions reveal hidden conceptions; the revealer must be in utmost clarity. This is a methodological guideline for constructing definitions through division, emphasizing clarity and order.

From Attributes to Definitions: How the Intellect Builds Hadd and Rasm
Author describes further abstraction of essential and accidental attributes, and composition into definitions and demonstrative statements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the process by which the intellect abstracts essential and accidental attributes to form definitions (hadd) and descriptions (rasm), and distinguish when a statement is primary versus needing demonstration.

Core Idea
Definitions and demonstrations both arise from abstraction of universals from sense particulars.

This passage reveals the cognitive journey from sensory particulars to universal concepts, and then to two types of composition: definitions that explain a thing's essence, and propositions that may be self-evident or require proof. Understanding this process clarifies why some statements are immediately accepted while others need a middle term.

Guided Path
1
Trace the abstraction process
Start with sense perception of particulars; then the intellect abstracts universals like genus, species, differentia, and accidents (essential and accidental).
2
Identify the two types of composition
The passage mentions composition into explanatory statements (qawl sharh) for definitions/descriptions, and into decisive statements (qawl jazim) for propositions.
Hadd uses essential attributes; rasm uses accidental or proprium.
3
Distinguish primary truths from those needing a middle term
After composition, if the mind does not hesitate in judgment, the statement is primary (awwali). If hesitation occurs, a middle term (al-wasat) is required for demonstration.
Primary truths are self-evident; others are acquired through syllogism.
4
Recognize the indirect role of sense
Sense perceives only particulars; the intellect does the work of abstraction and composition. Sense aids only accidentally by providing raw material.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعتبرت الذاتية والعرضية بين الأوصاف والموصوفات في هذه المعاني الكلية فتجرَّدت لها الفصول والأجناس والأنواع والأعراض اللازمة والمفارقة. ثم أخذت في أنحاء التركيب بعضها على التركيب الخاص بالقول الشارح لمعنى الشيء كالحد والرسم، وبعضها بالتركيب الخاص بالقول الجازم فيما لم يتوقف في الحكم إليه بعد هذا التركيب كان أوليا. وما لم يتوقف فيه كان ذلك محتاجاً إلى بيان توسط : فهذا وجه من وجوه إعانة الحس في حصول الأوليات؛ وهو إعانة على سبيل العرض؛ إذ الحس لا يدرك إلا الشخصي لكن الشخصيات إذا استقرت في الخيال متأدية إليه من الحسّ أقبل العقل على تجريدها من الكم والكيف والأين وغير ذلك، ثم ألفها بعد ذلك بالإيجاب / والسلب فلاح له ما يجب أن يصدق به بذاته، وتوقف فيما [٣١٩,] ليس كذلك إلى حصول الوسط.
Then it considered essentiality and accidentally among the attributes and the described in these universal meanings, so the differentiae, genera, species, and necessary and accidental accidents became distinguished for it. Then it turned to the modes of composition: some in the composition specific to the explanatory statement of a thing's meaning, like definition (hadd) and description (rasm); and some in the composition specific to the decisive statement (qawl jazim) in which if the judgment after this composition did not pause, it was primary. And what did not pause in it required a medial exposition. So this is one aspect of the aid of sense in acquiring first principles; and it is an aid in an accidental way. For sense perceives only the particular; but when particulars settle in the imagination having been conveyed to it from sense, the intellect turns to abstracting them from quantity, quality, location, and so on, then composes them with affirmation and negation. Then what must be assented to by itself becomes apparent to it, and it pauses in what [٣١٩, – not such] until the middle term is obtained.
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of how the intellect processes universals after acquiring them. It first distinguishes essential (dhati) and accidental ('aradi) attributes among the universal meanings. From this, the differentiae (fusul), genera (ajnas), species (anwa'), and necessary and accidental accidents (a'rad lazimah wa mufariqah) become clear. Then the intellect engages in composition (tarkib). Two types of composition are mentioned: (1) composition into an explanatory statement (qawl sharh) that defines a thing's meaning, i.e., hadd (proper definition) and rasm (description); (2) composition into a decisive statement (qawl jazim), i.e., a proposition. If after composition the mind does not hesitate in judgment, it is a primary truth; if it does hesitate, a middle term (al-wasat) is needed for demonstration. This is one way the sense aids in acquiring first principles, albeit indirectly, because the sense perceives only particulars. Once particulars are stored in the imagination, the intellect abstracts them from accidental features (quantity, quality, location) and then composes them into affirmative or negative judgments. From this, self-evident truths become apparent, while others require a middle term.

القول الجازم
الوسط
الذاتية والعرضية

The intellect abstracts universals from sense particulars, then composes them into definitions or propositions; primary truths are those admitted without hesitation, while others require a middle term for demonstration.

Refuting the Infinite Regress Objection in Defining Definition
Author refutes the infinite regress objection by distinguishing potential from actual infinity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish potential from actual infinite regress and use this distinction to refute objections against defining logical terms.

Core Idea
Not all infinite regresses are impossible; potential regress is logically acceptable.

In this passage, the author defends the possibility of defining 'definition' against an objection that it leads to an infinite regress. The objector argues that if definition has a definition, then that definition would need a definition, ad infinitum, which is impossible. The author, following Ibn Sina, responds by distinguishing between potential and actual infinite regress, showing that only actual regress is problematic. This distinction is crucial for understanding the limits of definition in logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find the mu'tarid's argument in the Arabic. The objector claims that defining definition leads to an infinite chain (tasalsul) which is impossible. Underline the phrase 'إلى غير النهاية وذلك محال'.
The objector assumes the regress is actual.
2
Find the response
Locate the author's jawab. He says the definition of definition is bi al-quwwa (potential), not bi al-fi'l (actual). Also, he uses the analogy of defining shapes from a single principle.
The phrase 'بالقوة لا بالفعل' is key.
3
Analyze the distinction
Understand that potential infinity means the capacity to define unlimited items without actualizing them all. Actual infinity would require each definition to be fully realized, which is impossible.
The author says 'لا يلزم من كون الشيء بالقوة أن يكون بالفعل'.
4
Apply the analogy
The example of shapes (triangle, square, etc.) defined by a single rule (counting sides) shows that one can potentially define an infinite number of polygons without actually doing so. Similarly, one can potentially define definition without actual infinite regress.
This analogy demonstrates that potential infinite regress is not logically problematic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلمنا بأن هذا الكلام نوع من التكلُّف. وأما الاعتراض عليه وذلك إنكم قد حددتم بقولكم هذا الحد. ولو كان للحد حد لوجب أن يكون لحد الحد حد إلى غير النهاية؛ وذلك محال فإن من جملة ما قد مرّ الكلام فيه. وأما الشيء فإنه كان يقول في الجواب عنه ليس حدي الحدّ المطلق هو حدي لحد الحدّ بالفعل؛ إذ ليس الحد المطلق هو حد الحد. وإن كان حدي الحد المطلق حدا بالقوة لحد الحد؛ إذ حد الحد حد لكنه ليس بالفعل. فإن حد الحد ليس هو قولا دالا على الماهية كيف كان قولا دالا على ماهية الحد كما أن حد الإنسان ليس قولا دالا على الماهية كيف كان بل هو قول دال على ماهية الإنسان لكني إذا علمتُ حد الحد فقد يسهل أن أجد حد الحد لأن حد الحد لفظ مؤلف من جزأين كل واحد منهما حد. فإذا حصل حد أحد الجزأين حصل حد الجزء الآخر، فحصل حد الجملة لأنه مؤلف من حد الجزأين؛ فهذا من جملة ما أشار إليه الشيخ رحمه الله في الشفاء. وبالجملة فقولهم إنه ذاهب إلى غير النهاية وذلك محال في حيز المنع فإنه يمكن أن يكون لنا قدرة على تحديد أمور بلا نهاية من قانون واحد كتحديد الأشكال من قانون تعديد الأضلاع حتى يقال للمثلث إنه شكل يحيط به ثلاثة أضلع، وللمربع شكل يحيط به أربعة أضلاع هلم جرا. فإن ذلك بالقوة لا بالفعل ولا يلزم من كون الشيء بالقوة أن يكون بالفعل بل يمكن أن يكون بالقوة؛ ولا يكون بالفعل أصلا.
We know that this speech is a type of affectation. As for the objection against it, it is that you have defined by this definition. And if definition had a definition, it would be necessary for the definition of definition to have a definition ad infinitum; that is impossible, and this is among what has been previously discussed. As for the matter, he used to say in response: 'My definition of the absolute definition is not my definition of the definition of definition actually; since the absolute definition is not the definition of definition. Although my definition of the absolute definition is a potential definition of the definition of definition; since the definition of definition is a definition but not actually. For the definition of definition is not a statement indicating the quiddity in whatever way, but a statement indicating the quiddity of definition, just as the definition of man is not a statement indicating the quiddity in whatever way, but a statement indicating the quiddity of man. However, if I know the definition of definition, it becomes easy to find the definition of definition, because the definition of definition is a composite expression consisting of two parts each of which is a definition. So if the definition of one part is obtained, the definition of the other part is obtained, and thus the definition of the whole is obtained because it is composed of the definitions of the two parts.' This is among what the Shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) indicated in al-Shifa'. In summary, their statement that it leads to infinity and that is impossible is in the realm of denial, because it is possible for us to have the capacity to define an unlimited number of things from a single principle, like defining shapes from the principle of counting sides, such that it is said of the triangle that it is a shape enclosed by three sides, and of the square that it is a shape enclosed by four sides, and so on. For that is potential, not actual, and it does not follow from a thing being potential that it is actual; rather it can be potential and never become actual.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange where the author defends the possibility of defining 'definition' (hadd) against the objection that it leads to infinite regress. The objector argues that if 'definition' has a definition, then that definition would itself need a definition, ad infinitum, which is impossible. The author responds by citing a response from 'the Shaykh' (Ibn Sina): the definition of definition is a potential (bi al-quwwa) definition, not an actual (bi al-fi'l) one. The definition of definition is not a definition in the full actual sense, but a statement that indicates the quiddity of definition. The author then explains that knowing the definition of one part of a composite helps define the other part. He further clarifies that potential infinite series are not impossible, using the example of defining shapes by a single principle (counting sides): one can potentially define an infinite number of polygons, but this potentiality does not require actual existence. Therefore, the infinite regress is only potential and not actually problematic.

بالقوة
بالفعل
التسلسل

Key Takeaway
The infinite regress in defining definition is only potential, not actual, and therefore not logically impossible.

Defining the Senses of a Common Name
Author introduces the second tool and illustrates with the example of 'good'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to produce definitions that distinguish the different meanings of a common name in Islamic terminology.

Core Idea
Knowing a term is shared is not enough; you must define the differences.

The author emphasizes that the second tool is not a generative rule but a skill: the capacity to detail common, similar, and equivocal names. This lesson focuses on the active requirement to define the distinct senses of a mushtarak term. Using the example of 'good' (khayr) in Islamic ethics, we see how courage, justice, and the virtuous person are not identical in meaning—each requires a definition that reveals its specific category.

Guided Path
1
Identify a suspected common name
Choose a term that appears in multiple Islamic disciplines or contexts. For example, the word ‘ʿilm’ can mean knowledge or a flag.
2
List its distinct applications
Write down the different things the term is applied to, e.g., in knowledge vs. a physical banner.
3
Define each sense using genus and differentia
For each application, determine the broader category (jins) and what sets it apart (fasl). For ‘ʿilm’ as knowledge: genus is ‘attribute’, differentia is ‘that which informs’.
If a full hadd is difficult, at least find a distinctive property (khāṣṣa).
4
Compare definitions to confirm difference
Check whether the definitions share the same genus or differentia. If they are not the same, the term is indeed mushtarak.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ب] وأما الآلة الثانية فهي القدرة على تفصيل الاسم المشترك والمتشابه والمتشكك؛ وهذا ليس قانوناً كالوضع أي بحيث يولد مقدمات بل إنما منفعته ما سَيَرِدُ بعد ذكره. ولا يجب أن يقتصر على أن يعلم أن لفظ كذا لفظ مشترك بل أن تكون له قدرة على إيراد حدود ما يشترك فيه للحدود التي تدل على مباينة بعضها البعض : فلا نقول مثلا إن الخير لا يقال على الشجاعة والعدل والعفة والمُصح والمحصن بمعنى واحد فقط بل وأن تبين كيفية ذلك فتبين مثلا أن الشجاعة والعدل يشير على أنها كيفية للخير، والمصح والمحصن على أنه فاعل للكيفية. وأما القوانين النافعة في معرفة أن الاسم الواقع على أشياء كثيرة تقع عليها وهي ذوات ماهيات وحقائق مختلفة أو تقع عليها بمعنى واحد؛ فمنها إن كان للشيء ضد فينظر هل الأشياء المعدودة مضادة للأشياء المتفقة في ذلك الاسم هي واحدة في الاسم أو مختلفة: فإن وجدها مختلفة الاسم في أول الأمر سهل عليه الوقوف على أن الاسم اسم مشترك، وإن لم يجدها مختلفة الأسماء فقد تعذر عليه. فإنه لا يمتنع أن يكون اسم مشترك وبإزائه اسم مشترك كالمضاد له، مثال الأول أن الاسم الحاد يقع على السيف وعلى الصوت. ويوجد له من حيث يقع على الصوت مضاد مخصوص باسم النقل، ومن حيث يقع على السيف مضاد مخصوص باسم الكليل وجداهما مختلفان؛ فيكون الحاد في السيف والصوت باشتراك الاسم، وعلى هذا في الغير من الصور. وأما مثال الثاني فهو أن يكون المضاد واحدي الاسم المشترك كما يقال صوت صاف ويقال صوت كدر، فهنا لا ينتفع فيه بذلك القانون. ولا يوجد من جهة التسمية مخلص غير الشبهة بل الحد والماهية والعلامة والخاصة هي التي تدل في أمثالها على الاشتراك. فإن الصفاء لو كان له فيهما معنًى واحد لكان مدركة حاسة واحدة لكن ليس كذلك بل يدرك أحدهما السمع، والآخر البصر. وعلى هذا في الغير من الصور، فهذه قوانين من جهة التضاد؛ فإن لم يكن للشيء مقابل بل بحسب التضاد يكون له مقابل على حسب التناقض البسيط
[B] As for the second tool, it is the ability to detail the common name (mushtarak), the similar (mutashābih), and the equivocal (mutashakkik); and this is not a rule like a postulate such that it generates premises, but rather its benefit is what will come after its mention. And one should not limit oneself to knowing that a certain expression is a common expression, but rather one should have the ability to produce definitions of what it is common in, with definitions that indicate the differences among them: so we do not say, for example, that 'good' (khayr) is said of courage, justice, chastity, and the good man (muslih?) and the virtuous (muhsin?) in only one meaning, but rather to explain how that is, so one explains, for example, that courage and justice indicate that they are a quality (kayfiyya) of the good, and the good man and virtuous are an agent (fā‘il) of the quality. As for the useful rules for knowing whether a name that applies to many things applies to them as things with different essences and realities or applies to them with one meaning: among them is that if a thing has a contrary (ḍidd), then one looks: are the enumerated things contrary to the things agreeing in that name one in name or different? If one finds them different in name at the outset, it becomes easy for him to ascertain that the name is a common name (mushtarak); and if he does not find them different in names, then it becomes difficult for him. For it is not impossible that a common name has a common name as its contrary, like the example of the first: the name 'ḥādd' (sharp) applies to the sword and to sound. And for it, insofar as it applies to sound, there is a specific contrary named 'naqil' (dull?), and insofar as it applies to the sword, a specific contrary named 'kalīl' (blunt); and he finds them different; so 'ḥādd' in the sword and sound is by common name (ishtirāk al-ism), and similarly for other cases. As for the second example, it is when the contrary is one common name, as one says 'clear sound' (ṣawt ṣāf) and 'turbid sound' (ṣawt kadar); here one does not benefit from that rule. And there is no deliverance from naming except through suspicion, but rather definition (ḥadd), essence (māhiyya), sign (‘alāma), and property (khāṣṣa) are what indicate in such cases the commonality. For if 'clarity' (ṣafā’) had in both the same meaning, then it would be perceived by a single sense, but it is not so; rather, one is perceived by hearing, the other by sight. And similarly for other cases. These are rules concerning contrariety; and if a thing has no opposite, then according to contrariety it has an opposite according to simple negation.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is definitional and explanatory, presenting the second tool in dialectic: the capacity to analyze common (mushtarak), similar (mutashābih), and equivocal (mutashakkik) names. The author clarifies that this tool is not a generative rule (qānūn) that produces premises, but its benefit will be explained later. The skill required is not merely knowing that a term is shared, but being able to give definitions showing the differences among the things it names. For example, 'good' (khayr) is said of courage, justice, chastity, and the good person—but not in one meaning; rather, courage and justice are qualities (kayfiyyāt) of good, while the good person is an agent (fā‘il) of that quality. The author then provides useful rules (qawānīn) for determining whether a name applies to things with different essences (common name) or one meaning. One rule uses contraries (ḍidd): if the things named have contraries, check whether those contraries are one name or different. If they are different, the original name is likely common. Example: 'ḥādd' (sharp) applies to sword and sound; its contrary for sound is 'naqīl' (dull?), for sword is 'kalīl' (blunt); since the contraries differ, 'ḥādd' is common. The second case is when the contrary is itself a common name (e.g., 'clear sound' vs. 'turbid sound'—both 'clear' there? Actually 'clear' might have different senses for hearing and sight). In that situation, the rule fails, and one must resort to definition (ḥadd), essence (māhiyya), sign (‘alāma), and property (khāṣṣa). For instance, 'clarity' (ṣafā’) if it had a single meaning would be perceived by one sense, but it is not: one aspect is heard, another seen. Thus, the true test of commonality lies in conceptual analysis, not just names. The passage concludes that these are rules based on contrariety; if there is no opposite, one uses simple negation.

Key Terms

متشابه
متشكك
حد
خاصة

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it insufficient to merely know that a term is a common name?
A) Because the term might be equivocal by analogy
B) Because one must be able to produce definitions showing the differences
C) Because the rule of contraries is more useful
D) Because common names are never truly shared

Key Takeaway
The second tool requires active definitional work, not just passive recognition, to distinguish the meanings of a common name.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the Arabic word 'imām' (إمام), which can refer to a prayer leader, a caliph, or a book. Write a short definition for each sense, showing how they differ in genus and differentia.
?
In a fiqh context, the term 'ribā' (ربا) is applied to different types of increase. Identify at least two distinct meanings (e.g., ribā al-faḍl and ribā al-nasī'a) and define each using the categories of 'contract' or 'exchange'.

Using Contraries to Detect Homonymy
Author explains the rule of contraries with examples of 'sharp' and 'clarity'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to use the rule of contraries to determine whether a name is a common name (mushtarak) in Islamic terminology.

Core Idea
When contraries have different names, the original term is likely common.

In this lesson, we explore a practical rule from the passage: if a term applies to multiple things, check the contraries of those things. If the contraries are expressed by different words, the term is probably a mushtarak. The author illustrates with 'ḥādd' (sharp) for sword and sound. However, the rule has limits—when the contrary itself is a common name, we must turn to definition and property, as with 'clarity' (ṣafā’).

Guided Path
1
Identify a promising candidate term
Choose a term that seems to have multiple applications, e.g., 'ḥādd' for sword and sound.
2
List the things it applies to
Write down the distinct objects: sword and sound.
3
Find the contrary for each application
For each object, determine its opposite. For sword, the opposite of sharp is 'blunt' (kalīl). For sound, the opposite of sharp is 'dull' (naqil).
These contraries must be from the same domain.
4
Check if contraries have different names
If the contraries are expressed by different words (kalīl vs. naqil), then the original term is likely mushtarak.
5
If contraries share a name, rely on definitions
When the contrary is itself a common name (e.g., 'clear' applied to sound and sight, contrary 'turbid'?), the rule fails. In that case, use definitions (ḥadd) and properties (khāṣṣa) to decide.
The author's example of 'clarity' (ṣafā’) shows that a single apparent meaning must be tested by sense perception and conceptual analysis.

The Law of Opposites for Detecting Shared Names
Author introduces the law of opposites with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the law of opposites to determine whether a name is shared across multiple contexts in Islamic logic.

Core Idea
Different opposites reveal shared names; identical opposites require deeper definitional analysis.

The law of opposites is one of the primary tools in Islamic logic for detecting shared names. By comparing the opposites of the things named, one can immediately see if the name carries different meanings. This lesson examines the test with clear examples from the tradition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opposite test
Identify the name and the multiple things it applies to. For each application, determine the specific opposite (ḍidd).
The opposite must be a genuine contrary, not just a negation.
2
Compare the opposites
If the opposites are different names (e.g., 'blunt' for sword, 'dull' for sound), the name is shared. If they are the same, the test fails.
The text uses the example of 'ḥād' (sharp) for sword and sound.
3
Recognize when the test fails
If the opposite is the same (e.g., 'clear' for sound and color have opposite 'muddy'), then the law is not beneficial; one must turn to definitions, essences, and properties.
This shows the limits of a single test.
4
Apply to an Islamic example
Consider the name 'qadīm' (old/eternal) applied to Allah (eternal) and to an ancient manuscript (old). The opposite of eternal is 'ḥādith' (originated); the opposite of old is 'jadīd' (new). Since the opposites differ, the name is shared.
This example illustrates the test in the context of Islamic theology.

Source Text

فتبين مثلا أن الشجاعة والعدل يشير على أنها كيفية للخير، والمُصح والمُحصن على أنه فاعل للكيفية. وأما القوانين النافعة في معرفة أن الاسم الواقع على أشياء كثيرة تقع عليها وهي ذوات ماهيات وحقائق مختلفة أو
